    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dc8c023d-bbbd-48bf-8be7-cf29f54c187c'

<span id="freeTextContainer14746355621553055073"><i>Dear reader</i>,<br/><br/>The word "carnivorous," which appears in the title of this book, means "meat-eating," and once you have read such a bloodthirsty word, there is no reason to read any further.   <span id="freeText14746355621553055073" style="display:none"><i>Dear reader</i>,<br /><br />The word "carnivorous," which appears in the title of this book, means "meat-eating," and once you have read such a bloodthirsty word, there is no reason to read any further. This carnivorous volume contains such a distressing story that consuming any of its contents would be far more stomach-turning than even the most imbalanced meal.<br /><br />To avoid causing discomfort, it would be best if I didn't mention any of the unnerving ingredients of this story, particularly a confusing map, an ambidextrous person, an unruly crowd, a wooden plank, and Chabo the Wolf Baby.<br /><br />Sadly for me, my time is filled with researching and recording the displeasing and disenchanting lives of the Baudelaire orphans. But your time might be better filled with something more palatable, such as eating your vegetables, or feeding them to someone else.<br /><br /><i>With all due respect</i>,<br /><i>Lemony Snicket</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14746355621553055073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/686102-why-is-a-man-with-equally-strong-arms-and">Why is a man with equally strong arms and legs be considered a freak? Many people have this. Heck, some people in my school are like this!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_686102'><a id="like_count_community_question_686102" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/686102?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F324277.The_Carnivorous_Carnival">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6013712-rosie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1471285063i/6013712._UY100_CR19,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6013712-rosie">Rosie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi, This question as already been answered but I thought I would put my two cents in. I've just finished re-reading this book and I think the purpose <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi, This question as already been answered but I thought I would put my two cents in. I've just finished re-reading this book and I think the purpose of having the ambidextrous man being considered a freak is to highlight how ridiculous the idea of freaks is - something shown in the scene at towards the end where the crowd are calling Esme's suit and the man with pimples freaks even though they aren't part of the freaks and aren't freakish in any way. It fits with the whole series where the only sane characters seem to be the orphans and is just a silly reminder that the adults in the series aren't the most sensible of people. I'm likely overthinking things but that's what I got from the book this time around reading it. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237010391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15141554777194222975">Once again I get the chance to say (write?) the most glorious words in the English language: This is a particularly fantastic installment in the GREATEST SERIES OF ALL TIME.<br/><br/>In case you're new here or somehow able to ignore me doing the internet equivalent of nonstop screaming about this series: I LOVE THESE BOOKS SO MUCH.<br/><br/>This one is, as mentioned, particularly next-level at putting all other excuses for literature to shame. It breaks from the typical format. Our lil gang grows up. There's an exp</span>
  <span id="freeText15141554777194222975" style="display:none">Once again I get the chance to say (write?) the most glorious words in the English language: This is a particularly fantastic installment in the GREATEST SERIES OF ALL TIME.<br /><br />In case you're new here or somehow able to ignore me doing the internet equivalent of nonstop screaming about this series: I LOVE THESE BOOKS SO MUCH.<br /><br />This one is, as mentioned, particularly next-level at putting all other excuses for literature to shame. It breaks from the typical format. Our lil gang grows up. There's an exploration of moral absolutism, a questioning of whether anyone is truly good or evil, and whether evil acts can be motivated by pure intentions. There's a condemnation of normalcy, one which points out (TO A MAIN AUDIENCE OF CHILDREN MAY I REMIND YOU) that no one is normal and everyone's got something freakish about them.<br /><br />Also, there are fortune-tellers and inventions and disguises and Thai food and page repetition to mock déjà vu and, as always, some of the best world-building and narration of all time.<br /><br />IT'S A GREAT BOOK AND I HAVE A MIGRAINE SO I NEED TO STOP LOOKING AT A SCREEN NOW.<br /><br />Bottom line: If you haven't read these books yet and don't plan to in the immediate future, clearly you don't care about me AT ALL.</span>

<div id="review_2774040444" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774040444" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774040444?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774040444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer328955111333596571">In this installment, the Baudelaires arrive at Caligari Carnival after hitching a ride in Count Olaf’s trunk. Their plan, as usual, is to seek safety from Count Olaf, but they soon discover that there’s nowhere to go, and Count Olaf will be in the vicinity for some time to come. They take a huge chance by disguising themselves as freaks in order to participate in Caligari Carnival’s freak show (Violet and Clause as a two-headed freak, and Sunny as Chabo the Wolf Baby), which lands them working r</span>
  <span id="freeText328955111333596571" style="display:none">In this installment, the Baudelaires arrive at Caligari Carnival after hitching a ride in Count Olaf’s trunk. Their plan, as usual, is to seek safety from Count Olaf, but they soon discover that there’s nowhere to go, and Count Olaf will be in the vicinity for some time to come. They take a huge chance by disguising themselves as freaks in order to participate in Caligari Carnival’s freak show (Violet and Clause as a two-headed freak, and Sunny as Chabo the Wolf Baby), which lands them working right alongside Count Olaf.<br /><br />Now that the Baudelaires are in close quarters with Count Olaf and his troupe, they discover more interesting clues about V.F.D. and other more shocking facts regarding their parents. Will the childrens’ stealthy behavior pay off? Will they ever discover what happened to their parents?<br /><br /><i>“One of the most troublesome things in life is that what you do or do not want has very little to do with what does or does not happen.”</i><br /><br />This one had us on edge! The children are incredibly close to danger once again, working up close with Count Olaf and his nasty accomplices. This added a lot of suspense. There were slow parts, but it didn’t take long to pick up, and we found ourselves racing to discover what would happen with the children this time around.<br /><br /><i>“Fate is like a strange, unpopular restaurant, filled with odd waiters who bring you things you never asked for and don’t always like.”</i><br /><br />We appreciated the new characters in this installment. Madame Lulu is an interesting new character that ties in with a few of the other books. She’s willing to help the Baudelaires, which is rare and often ends disastrously.<br /><br />Comparable to the other books, there are many new vocabulary words introduced for children to learn in this installment including: haughtily, depict, contortionist, eavesdropping, ambidextrous, and dilemma to name a few.<br /><br />The ending had us quite shocked, and like last time, we had to move right on to the next book. Overall, we really enjoyed this one.<br /><br />4****</span>
  <a data-text-id="328955111333596571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135790714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer792737073042689449">The children arrive hidden in the trunk of Count Olaf's car. A new turn of events - they know where Olaf is and it's them who are in disguise.<br/><br/>The good-evil, noble-villain theme expands. The children are the spies. In addition they meet and join the circus 'freaks' who they see put to the test - decent people in a hard place offered difficult choices - will they act like noble people or villains? The circus freaks are a test case, an example, perhaps an illustration of how Olaf's hench-people & p</span>
  <span id="freeText792737073042689449" style="display:none">The children arrive hidden in the trunk of Count Olaf's car. A new turn of events - they know where Olaf is and it's them who are in disguise.<br /><br />The good-evil, noble-villain theme expands. The children are the spies. In addition they meet and join the circus 'freaks' who they see put to the test - decent people in a hard place offered difficult choices - will they act like noble people or villains? The circus freaks are a test case, an example, perhaps an illustration of how Olaf's hench-people &amp; perhaps Olaf himself descended by degrees into villainy.<br /><br />We are tantalized with more mysteries and more possible solutions - we discover the secret that has allowed Olaf to find the children time and again...<br /><br />And at the end the children face danger and hard choices themselves.<br /><br />Continues with the familiar humour, word games etc. Also, Sunny continues to grow, expands her vocabulary, and starts to show an interest in cooking - which becomes her 'thing' in later books. <br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br /><br />....</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8984851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6853347954961577522">My daughter and I adored the entire series, but this episode is my favorite. It contains perhaps the funniest of Lemony Snicket's etymological digressions. It marks the point where the larger story begins to evolve, where the traumatized young Baudelaire orphans first turn the tables on their arch-nemesis, Count Olaf. And it's also a point where both the orphans and the story mature, evolving from a good-vs-evil fairy tale of morbid victimhood into a subtle study of moral complexity.<br/><br/>It's a pity </span>
  <span id="freeText6853347954961577522" style="display:none">My daughter and I adored the entire series, but this episode is my favorite. It contains perhaps the funniest of Lemony Snicket's etymological digressions. It marks the point where the larger story begins to evolve, where the traumatized young Baudelaire orphans first turn the tables on their arch-nemesis, Count Olaf. And it's also a point where both the orphans and the story mature, evolving from a good-vs-evil fairy tale of morbid victimhood into a subtle study of moral complexity.<br /><br />It's a pity that so many people who begin this series give up after three or four volumes. But if you make it through The Carniverous Carnival, you won't want to stop.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108599050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3241246252765502212"><b>JANUARY 2017 RE-READ</b><br/><br/>Bumping this up from 4 stars to 5. I last read this when it first came out in 2002! So that was FIFTEEN YEARS AGO. God I feel old. For some reason I had it in my head that I didn't enjoy this one as much as others in the series, but I was clearly mistaken because this is a great instalment. I like how books 2-7 involve Count Olaf in disguises trying to fool the Baudelaires, and books 8 and 9 involve the Baudelaires in disguises trying to fool Count Olaf. Madame Lulu is a cool</span>
  <span id="freeText3241246252765502212" style="display:none"><b>JANUARY 2017 RE-READ</b><br /><br />Bumping this up from 4 stars to 5. I last read this when it first came out in 2002! So that was FIFTEEN YEARS AGO. God I feel old. For some reason I had it in my head that I didn't enjoy this one as much as others in the series, but I was clearly mistaken because this is a great instalment. I like how books 2-7 involve Count Olaf in disguises trying to fool the Baudelaires, and books 8 and 9 involve the Baudelaires in disguises trying to fool Count Olaf. Madame Lulu is a cool character, FINALLY the children are learning even more about V.F.D., the carnival setting is fun...just so many great things happening here. Shout out to one of the freak show performers: Kevin the ambidextrous man! Also some great and not-so-subtle messages about prejudice. I just love Daniel Handler's writing style, and his decision to create a pen-name who is also a character. Bravo.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3241246252765502212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13879182879684048759" style="display:none">Just dipping into this series to find out what it is all about. Maybe I should have tried book 1 first but <br />I happened on this one by accident. <br />I think if I had read this when I was a child I would have loved it. Despite all the terrible things that <br />happen to the Baudelaires there is always a feeling that they will find a way out and since I hated <br />suspense back then this would have suited me down to the ground. <br />As an adult I enjoyed the dryness of the narrative, the slightly snarky comments and expressions <br />which are certainly intended for the grown up readers, not the children. (Not too sure though about <br />some of the content especially the treatment of "the freaks.")<br />Altogether I can certainly see why the series has so many followers although I do not feel the <br />immediate need to rush out and read any more myself. </span>

<div id="review_788025237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/788025237" />
    <a title="Deborah Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus"><img alt="Deborah Markus" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/788025237?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Markus" href="/user/show/954028-deborah-markus">Deborah Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954028-deborah-markus?shelf=coffee-break-for-my-brain">coffee-break-for-my-brain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer788025237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7599154861977753098">Snicket engages in some serious moral wrangling in this volume, and forces the reader to do the same. At a crucial moment, the Baudelaire orphans meet a woman who wants to be a good, strong person -- but because her motto is "give people what they want," she can always be manipulated by villains, and always tells herself that she <i>must</i> be a good person, because isn't giving people what they want a good thing to do? The simple answer, "Not if they want bad things!" never seems to occur to her.<br/><br/>It o</span>
  <span id="freeText7599154861977753098" style="display:none">Snicket engages in some serious moral wrangling in this volume, and forces the reader to do the same. At a crucial moment, the Baudelaire orphans meet a woman who wants to be a good, strong person -- but because her motto is "give people what they want," she can always be manipulated by villains, and always tells herself that she <i>must</i> be a good person, because isn't giving people what they want a good thing to do? The simple answer, "Not if they want bad things!" never seems to occur to her.<br /><br />It occurs to the Baudelaires, of course. Partly because they're nobler than she is. Partly because they desperately need her help. In the course of trying to persuade her to give them what they <i>need,</i> they're forced to admit that in spite of their best intentions, they seem to be sliding down a slippery moral slope:<br /><br /><i>"Haven't you ever found yourself doing something you never thought you'd do?"<br /><br />"I guess so," Klaus said, and turned to his sisters. "Remember when we stole those keys from Hal, at the Library of Records? I never thought I'd be a thief."<br /><br />"Flynn," Sunny said, which meant something like, "And I never thought I would become a violent person, but I engaged in a sword fight with Dr. Orwell."<br /><br />"We've all done things we never thought we'd do," Violet said, "but we always had a good reason."<br /><br />"Everybody thinks they have a good reason," Olivia said.</i><br /><br />Ouch.<br /><br />This is the first book in the Series of Unfortunate Events to end on a really suspenseful cliffhanger. I'm glad I wasn't an early adopter with these books. I would have hated to have to wait a whole year to see what happened next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7599154861977753098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10195569076941685031">3 Stars.<br/><br/>My binge read of this series continues. If you've been following my reviews, you may notice that the ratings have been dropping, mainly because I feel that the story is becoming a little too repetitive and that there would be some really simple solutions to the children's problems. I don't want to spoil anything, but at the start, Violet, Klaus and Sunny are near Olaf's unattended car and instead of thinking "Let's use Violet's mechanical skills to hot-wire this car and Klaus' knowledge </span>
  <span id="freeText10195569076941685031" style="display:none">3 Stars.<br /><br />My binge read of this series continues. If you've been following my reviews, you may notice that the ratings have been dropping, mainly because I feel that the story is becoming a little too repetitive and that there would be some really simple solutions to the children's problems. I don't want to spoil anything, but at the start, Violet, Klaus and Sunny are near Olaf's unattended car and instead of thinking "Let's use Violet's mechanical skills to hot-wire this car and Klaus' knowledge of all things to drive our way to freedom, hurrah!" Instead they head TOWARDS the villains, then stuff got weird, and at the end, it was obvious that Olaf knew (I won't say what, because spoilers) but then the children just... go with it? Even when I thought that they knew that he knew. Strange. At times, it just feels like the characters are being pushed into a predestined plot even though they've evolved beyond it, so it feels stiff and wrong. <br /><br />I'm still finishing this series, but my hopes are going down that there will ever be satisfactory answers and the plots aren't as intriguing and fascinating as the earlier books. Well, next is book 10.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10195569076941685031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12436941646610100912"><b>There are almost as many kinds of libraries as there are kinds of readers. </b><br/><br/>It feels like i'm heading into that home stretch with the Baudelaire children and i know there isn't many books left in this series but i cannot wait to finally learn what they've been trying to find out for a few books now. <br/><br/>Book nine sees the Baudelaire children heading towards a carnival after hiding out in the trunk of count Olaf's car as they had no other option at the end of book eight.   <span id="freeText12436941646610100912" style="display:none"><b>There are almost as many kinds of libraries as there are kinds of readers. </b><br /><br />It feels like i'm heading into that home stretch with the Baudelaire children and i know there isn't many books left in this series but i cannot wait to finally learn what they've been trying to find out for a few books now. <br /><br />Book nine sees the Baudelaire children heading towards a carnival after hiding out in the trunk of count Olaf's car as they had no other option at the end of book eight. I can't believe that count Olaf or any of his workers did not think to check the trunk at any point of their journey and i consider the children very lucky that they didn't <br /><br />This whole V.F.D business is really starting to get to me because i need to know what it means and every chance the kids get to finding out they are either interrupted or don't get a chance to find out anything. However we have some developments with them finding a symbol and learning that some members of the V.F.D. are currently at the carnival. <br /><br /><b> But the sad truth is that the truth is sad, and that what you want does not matter. A series of unfortunate events can happen to anyone, no matter what they want </b><br /><br />Ok i need to know what Mr. Poe is doing because isn't he the one that's supposed to be looking after these children and is supposed to know where they are at every given moment. I'm sorry to say i believe hes let these children down because there has been no evidence to suggest that he's even remotely looking for them so there completely on their own at this point. <br /><br />There were some major plot developments in this one finally and i can't wait to find out more in the coming books to hopefully finally see these kids have somewhat of an ending to their unfortunate story because i think these kids really do need something at the end of this. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7756943333558390519"><br/>This addition to the series, as well as the previous one, is a bit darker than the rest of the series. The last book had a creepy vibe, while this one has a downright miserable vibe. I think maybe it's because carnivals, circuses and freakshows, have a creepy, dark vibe to them already, and then it's mixed with the incredibly sad lives of the Baudelaires.<br/><br/>I'm slightly frustrated by how almost none of the mysteries are explained so far, while new questions just keeps on piling up - but of course t</span>
  <span id="freeText7756943333558390519" style="display:none"><br />This addition to the series, as well as the previous one, is a bit darker than the rest of the series. I think maybe it's because carnivals, circuses and freakshows, have a creepy, dark vibe to them already, and then it's mixed with the incredibly sad lives of the Baudelaires.<br /><br />I'm slightly frustrated by how almost none of the mysteries are explained so far, while new questions just keeps on piling up - but of course there's still four books left.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_8030789'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8030789-a-series-of-unfortunate-events"><img alt="A Series of Unfortunate Events" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/book/111x148-bcc042a9c91a29c1d680899eff700a03.png" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zsQiJqWyG6oINzbYsAQlzghVgk6XPGRD26CQe2FHim1pb93OyTdLkrSCjMlb1ZjVe68CdMDp0QMZnKXgZVO3gA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qi3OITnMl+ErpNhfLRVpPCXhuLNli86cRpxR8y15yOINhjHJVUnH2ZcRYk7GxNQnVhs4iTJee9yEoGRoKW31Dw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
